DETAILED RESULTS 
 
Part I. ISSUER 
Level of the issuer’s ESG commitments:  
As of September 2015, DC Water’s overall commitments on ESG issues continue to be considered robust and its policies 
cover ESG issues homogeneously. 
Domain Comments 
Opinion 
assessment 
level 
Environment 
DC Water’s environmental strategy is clearly defined and integrated in the DC Water Strategic Plan 2020. 
DC Water’s commitments regarding the minimization of its impacts due to energy use are particularly 
advanced, and a quantitative target of green energy provision is defined. 
Protection of biodiversity, waste management and reduction of water consumption may be better 
addressed with a more preventive perspective. 
Weak 
Limited 
Robust 
Advanced 
Social 
The social dimension is well addressed by DC Water, which has deployed relevant policies aimed at 
managing responsibly its human resources, human rights, customer and supplier relations and community 
involvement. In particular, career development and efforts to promote Minority/Women Business 
Enterprise (M/WBE) contracting and local hiring in DC Water projects have improved since the last review
 
(June 2014).  
Procurement and quality of service policies have been adopted to promote responsible relations with 
contractors and customers and integration of sustainability factors with contractors.

oversight, control and disclosure on audit and internal control.

Stakeholder-related ESG controversies: 
- Frequency: as of July 1 st 2015, DC Water faces occasional allegations: the company is currently involved in 5 
stakeholder-related ESG controversies. Two cases concern the respect of labor practices by contractors, one case is 
related to the prevention of pollution (damaged pipe) and two cases concern racial discrimination. 
- Severity: The level of severity ranges from significant to high, major cases (3/5) are considered as significant level in 
severity despite their nature as allegations 
- Responsiveness: DC Water is reactive: the issuer reports transparently on all the cases, and remedial actions have 
been taken in response to 4/5 cases, including the cooperation with impacted stakeholders, the legal process is still in 
progress on the remaining case. 
Based on assessment of severity, responsiveness and frequency, Vigeo considers that DC Water’s ability to mitigate ESG 
controversy to be robust (sources: Factiva research and Company's sources).

Part II. PROJECT 
Use of proceeds 
The net proceeds of issuance will be used to finance a portion of the cons truction and development of the tunnels 
associated with the DC Cle an Rivers Project, the “Eligible Project”, which promotes water quali ty, such as reducing 
Combined Sewer Overflow (CSO) into the Potomac and Anacost ia Rivers, climate resilien ce and quality of life. The 
Eligible Project has been independentl y assessed by Vigeo on Environmental, Social and Governance (ESG) criteria 
integration. 
 
/g120 Project description 
The District of Columbia ’s National Pollutant Discharge Elimination System (NPDES) permit, issued by the U.S. EPA 
requires the preparation of a Long-Term Control Plan (LTCP): the DC Clean Rivers Pr oject ($2.6 billion), a plan that 
aims at controlling CSO discharges to the area wa terways (schedule: 2005-2025), implemented under a Federal 
Consent Decree among: U.S. EPA, US Department of Justice, D istrict of Columbia and DC Water. Included in 
wastewater treatment services , the DC Clean Rivers Project is a larg e scale infrastructure  and support program 
managed by DC Water. It re lies on the construction of large tunnels designed to capture CSO during heavy rainfalls 
before reaching waterways and transport it to the Blue Plains Advanced Wastewater Treatment Plant for treatment. 
The project is scheduled according to two stages: 
- First stage: Anacostia River tunnel  - project underway; on schedule for completion in 2018 
- Second stage: Potomac River and Rock Creek tunnels and related infrastructures - project underway; on 
schedule for completion in 2025 
As of July 2015, the first segment of  the Anacostia Tunnel, the Blue Plains  Tunnel, has been finished and the First 
Street and Anacostia River Tunnel are under construction. 
 
/g120 Environmental and social outcomes 
Three core environmental and social outcomes have been identified and associated objecti ves are visible, precise, 
dated, measurable and relevan t. In addition, effective results have been observed for each, based on the outcome 
assessment of the project impact reporting. 
 
Water Quality 
Outcome Protect people from possible harmful substances in wastewater by improvement of water quality 
Final objective Reduce CSO into the District's waterways - the Anacostia and Potomac Rive rs and Rock Creek – by 
96% system wide (98% in Anacostia river) 
Impact reporting  
(outcome assessment 
- July 2015) 
% Reduction in CSO Overflow Volume 
% of CSO are effectively reduced since the project beginning: 40% of reduced CSO in 2015 compared 
with the situation without the project in 1996. Results for each river are in line with that result, except 
for the Rock Creek where only 12% of CSO ar e reduced, because of  the project progr ess and 
scheduling.  
The evolution between the FY2014 Green Bond report and the current review is stable.
 
Construction progress of tunnel 
The construction of the Blue Plains Tunnel is fi nished, with 24,207 linear feet minded. The Anacostia 
River Tunnel i s under construction and the First Street Tunnel is at design stage. Thus, 61% of the 
overall tunnel length has been co nstructed, which is in line with  the actual spend against budget since 
the inception of the project. 
The construction progress h as increased between the current 
review and the FY2014 Green Bond 
report, where only 46% of the Blue Plains Tunnel was mined.

Climate Resilience 
Outcome Protect people from exposure to harmful flood water;  re- population of homes quarantined through 
sewage-contaminated flood water; rehabilitation of flood prone areas of the district 
Final objective Relieve and mitigate flooding 
Impact reporting  
(outcome assessment 
- July 2015) 
Description of flood relief and mitigation programs  
More than $102 million have been spent, i.e. only 14% of th e total flood relief and mitigation program 
budget ($714 million), focusing on McMillan Stormwater Storage (99% of budget spent) and Irving 
Street Green Infrastructure (97% budget spent) in line with the construct ion progress. The climate 
resilience efforts are concentrated on relevant areas. 
The fund spend on flood relief and mitigation  programs has increased between the current review and 
the FY2014 Green Bond report, where only 7% of the budget was spent. 
 
 
Quality of life 
Outcome 
Reduce contaminants and pollutants flow into the waterway to restore a safe and healthy environment 
for reestablishment and promotion of river-based societal recreational activity and industry and for 
aquatic ecosystem 
Final objective Remove contaminants and pollutants (nitrogen, phos phorus and suspended solids) in the District's 
waterways 
Impact reporting  
(outcome assessment 
- July 2015) 
Nitrogen and phosphorus removal 
Nitrogen and Phosphorous are effectively removed in the waterway, with respectively 82% and 97% of 
removal between influent and effluent quantities at Blue Plains and 40% of removal for both at CSO 
Outfalls (in lbs). Initial expected objective for nitrogen remo val was at least 50% of reduction, which is 
fully achieved at Blue Plains. 
The nitrogen removal has increased between the current review and the FY2014 Green Bond report, 
where 78% was achieved. The phosphorous removal is stable. 
Suspended solids removal 
Suspended solids are effectively removed in the waterway, with 99% of removal between influent and 
effluent quantities at Blue Plains and 40% of removal at CSO Outfalls (in lbs).  
The suspended solids removal is  stable between the current review and the FY2014 Green Bond 
report. 
 
 
Management of proceeds 
The Green Bond proceeds of the Series 2015 A Green Bonds for DC Clean Rivers Project will be deposited in a segregated 
account of the Construction Fund for the Series 2015 A Project established and maintained under the Indenture that secures 
the Bonds.  
Pending allocation to the DC Clean Rivers Project, the net proceeds of the issuance of the Bonds will be allocated to a sub-
portfolio and the Issuer will invest such net proceeds, in cash or any other liquid marketable instruments as permitted under its 
bond indenture.

METHODOLOGY  
In Vigeo’s view, ESG factors are intertwined and complementary and cannot be separated when assessing the management of 
sustainability in any organization or in any activity, including the issuance of green bonds. In this sense, we write an opinion on 
the issuer’s responsibility as a corporate organization, and on the objectives, the management and the reporting of the project 
financed by this bond. 
 
Vigeo’s methodology to define and to assess corporate ESG performance is based on criteria aligned with public international 
standards, in compliance with the ISO 26000 guidelines, and organized in 6 domains : Environment, Human Resources, Human 
Rights, Community Involvement, Business Behavior and Corporate Governance. The evaluation framework has been 
customized regarding material issues, based on the Vigeo’s Waste & Water and Local Authority assessment framework, local 
specificities and presence of recurrent controversies impacting the sector. 
 
 
Part I. ISSUER 
Level of the issuer’s ESG commitments:  
DC Water has been assessed by Vigeo on the commitments to 22 relevant ESG drivers.   
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
DC Water’s ESG policies have been assessed by Vigeo on the level of commitment, through the relevance of their:  
- Visibility: visibility of the commitments and policies towards stakeholders 
- Content: exhaustiveness and relevance of the commitments and policies with respect to action steps 
- Ownership: adequacy of hierarchical backing (person or structure in charge of the policy) 
 
/g131 Scale for assessment of commitments: Advanced, Robust, Limited, Weak. 
 
Vigeo’s review uses information provided by DC Water (internal documentation and interviews), press content providers and 
stakeholders (partnership with Factiva Dow Jones: access to the content of 28,500 publications worldwide from reference 
financial newspapers to sector-focused magazines, local publications or Non-Government Organizations).  
DC Water processes and performance in terms of corporate responsibility have not been subjected to Vigeo Rating’s 
complete process of rating and benchmark. 
 
Stakeholder-related ESG controversies: 
A controversy is information, a flow of information, or contradictory opinions that are public, documented and traceable, 
allegation against an issuer on corporate responsibility issues. Such allegations can relate to tangible facts, be an interpretation of 
these facts, or constitute an allegation on unproven facts.

Vigeo provides an opinion on companies’ controversies risk mitigation based on the analysis of three factors :  
- Severity: the more a controversy will relate to stakeholder’s fundamental interests, will prove actual corporate 
responsibility in its occurrence, and will have adverse impacts for stakeholders and the Company, the highest its 
severity. Severity assigned at corporate level will reflect the highest severity of all cases faced by the Company (scale: 
Minor, Significant, High, Critical); 
- Responsiveness: ability demonstrated by an issuer to dialogue with its stakeholders in a risk management perspective 
and based on explanatory, preventative, remediating or corrective measures. At corporate level, this factor will reflect 
the overall responsiveness of the Company for all cases faced (scale: Proactive, Remediate, Reactive, Non 
Communicative); 
- Frequency: reflects for each ESG challenge the number of controversies faced. At Corporate level, this factor reflects 
on the overall number of controversies faced and scope of ESG issues impacted (scale: Isolated, Occasional, Frequent, 
Persistent). 
 
/g131 Scale for assessment of ability to mitigate stakeholder-related ESG contro versies: Advanced, Robust, Limited, 
Weak. 
 
 
Part II. PROJECT 
Use of proceeds 
The use of proceeds requirements are defined to ensure that the funds raised are used to finance an eligible project and are 
traceable within the issuing organization, and include the management of proceeds.  
The environmental and social purpose of the bond’s associated eligible project has been precisely defined, with regard to DC 
Water’s commitments. The environmental and social benefits of the project have been described and assessed. 
ESG integration in the project 
DC Clean Rivers Project has been assessed by Vigeo on the implementation of 19 relevant ESG  drivers, according to a 
customized assessment framework, derived from the corporate assessment framework, focusing on the most relevant drivers 
regarding the financed project issues. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
Vigeo has appreciated a level of assurance for each criteria under analysis regarding the coherence of implementation at the 
Project level through: 
- Process: procedures, guidelines and measures in place to ensure all the commitments and policies can be 
implemented; 
- Means: resources available and implemented to put in place the commitments and policies; 
- Control: reporting systems, monitoring and external audit. 
 
/g131 Scale for assessment of implementation at project level: Advanced, Robust, Limited, Weak

Part III. REPORTING 
Reporting indicators are selected from existing indicators in use by DC Water enable annual reporting on fund allocation, 
environmental and social benefits and on responsible management of the project financed by the Green Bond proceeds, 
collected at project level. 
Vigeo has evaluated the relevance of these indicators according to three following principles: transparency, exhaustiveness and 
effectiveness: in order to provide an opinion on the issuer’s commitment and capacity to report on the green bond. 
/g131 Scale of level of assurance on reporting commitment on the project: Reasonable, Moderate, Weak
